<div id="tr1698529"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1698529"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> said that this film's theme deals with "Pain". For <a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005), it was on "Fear", while <a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008) deals on "Chaos".  </div>

<div id="tr2239501"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2239501"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
About a year before the film's release, <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> mentioned he was considering using a mixture of CGI and deleted scenes from <a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008) to have the Joker appear briefly. He ultimately decided it was disrespectful to <a href="/name/nm0005132">Heath Ledger</a>.  </div>

<div id="tr1770743"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1770743"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
While doing promotional interviews for the film, <a href="/name/nm0362766">Tom Hardy</a> stated that the most difficult parts of the movie to shoot were the fight scenes. Not because of the physicality of them, but because he was such a huge Batman fan growing up, that he said "it felt like I was beating up my childhood hero". However, he also said that despite his worship of the character, the moment <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> yelled "Action"!, Hardy just started throwing punches as hard as he could.  </div>

<div id="tr2049157"

  <a name="tr2049157"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
When Bruce Wayne traces the fake fingerprints that the Catwoman was wearing when she cracked his safe, the result shows a "Nikolai Ondrejko". This is the same name that was used by the Joker to author the fake obituary for the Mayor in <a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008).  </div>

<div id="tr1686831"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1686831"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0004266">Anne Hathaway</a> has said that she desperately coveted the role of Catwoman, and was a complete nervous wreck after her audition. The first time her agent phoned after her screen test, he said he had good news and asked if Hathaway was sitting down. Hathaway immediately screamed "I'm Catwoman!" and ran around the room in a frenzy. Unfortunately, her agent had to calm the actress down--he had called to let her know that she'd been invited to host the Academy Awards. Hathaway has said she was so shocked she went numb at the offer. Fortunately, shortly thereafter, her agent phoned again to let her know that she had been offered the part of Catwoman as well.  </div>

During the motorcycle chase scene, Bane is wearing a red helmet with black visor as well as a brown motorcycle jacket. This is the original costume Jason Todd took under his Red Hood persona, which is itself a callback to The Joker's original criminal identity.  </div>

<div id="tr1739549"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1739549"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> wanted <a href="/name/nm0182839">Marion Cotillard</a> so much for the role of Miranda Tate, that he modified the filming schedule to accommodate her pregnancy. When Nolan invited Cotillard for the film in 2010, she told him that she was pregnant, and didn't know if she would be able to do it, but Nolan decided to keep her in the film. Cotillard started filming just one month after giving birth, and Nolan also made room on-set for her family. In the last months of filming, Cotillard also shot another film at the same time in France, <a href="/title/tt2053425">Rust and Bone</a> (2012). She was flying back and forth between the U.S. and France to shoot both movies. During an interview for Vogue in August 2012, Nolan marveled at Cotillard's ability to do her job so soon after giving birth, calling it "amazing to see" and describing her as "Superwoman".  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

Bruce Wayne's doctor visit, in which the doctor lists off all the degenerative injuries to his body (lack of cartilage, scar tissue, et cetera) and the use of a mechanical knee brace, both are reminiscent of <a href="/name/nm1632388">Mark Waid</a>'s Justice League novel Kingdom Come (set in a hypothetical future), where an older Bruce Wayne requires the use of an exoskeleton to move, due to years of physical wear and tear on his body.  </div>

<div id="tr1840674"

  <a name="tr1840674"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
During one of the scenes involving the kangaroo court, Bane can be seen sitting in the rear of the courtroom quietly knitting. Given the numerous allusions to <a href="/name/nm0002042">Charles Dickens</a>' "A Tale of Two Cities" in the film, this is presumably an allusion to Madame Defarge and her practice of knitting while watching public guillotine executions.  </div>

<div id="tr1742574"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1742574"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The Batsuit consisted of 110 separate pieces. The base layer was made of a polyester mesh, utilized by the military and high-tech sports manufacturers due to its breathability and moisture-retaining properties; molded pieces of flexible urethane were then attached to the mesh to form the overall body armor plating. Carbon fiberpanels were placed inside the sections on the legs, chest and abdomen. The cowl was sculpted from a cast of <a href="/name/nm0000288">Christian Bale</a>'s face and head to become a perfect fit for Bale.  </div>

<div id="tr1874147"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1874147"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
During Bane's first encounter with Batman, Bane's footsteps on the steel grating of the walkways produce loud, heavy thuds while Batman's footsteps make little sound at all. This was done by the sound effects team to further contrast Bane's "brute" style from Batman's "stealth" method of combat.  </div>

According to Costume Designer <a href="/name/nm0376089">Lindy Hemming</a>, she took two years to design Bane's coat; it was inspired by a Swedish army jacket, and a French Revolution frock coat, to make Bane look equally dictatorial and revolutionary, "like an amalgam of all sorts of bits and pieces he cobbled together as he passed through some very remote places."  </div>

<div id="tr1707332"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1707332"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The nickname "Catwoman" is never spoken in the movie; rather newspaper articles and police files refer to her as "The Cat." This is in keeping with the original incarnation of the character (not yet named Selina Kyle) who was a jewel thief, and was known only as "The Cat" before becoming "The Catwoman." However, various official merchandise and marketing material refer to Selina Kyle as Catwoman when she is wearing her masked costume. Furthermore, the shooting script refers to Kyle as "Catwoman" when in costume.  </div>

<div id="tr1742577"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1742577"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In designing the Batwing, Production Designer <a href="/name/nm0189769">Nathan Crowley</a> approached it as if it were an actual military project, emphasizing the need for it to "fit into the same family as the Tumbler and the Batpod": he incorporated designs from military aircraft, including the Harrier Jump Jet, Bell Boeing V-22 Osprey and the Boeing AH-64 Apache.  </div>

<div id="tr1740221"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1740221"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
According to <a href="/name/nm0362766">Tom Hardy</a>, he based his voice for Bane on Bartley Gorman (1944 - 2002), an Irish Traveller who was the undefeated Bare-knuckle boxing champion of the United Kingdom: "The choice of the accent is actually a man called Bartley Gorman, who was a bare knuckle fighter, a Romani gypsy. So I wanted to underpin the Latin, but a Romani Latin opposed to Latino."  </div>

<div id="tr1748958"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1748958"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
On July 20, 2012 during a midnight screening for the film in Aurora, Colorado, a man entered the theater and opened fire. <a href="/name/nm4601595">James Holmes</a> ended up killing twelve people and injured fifty-eight. He was arrested outside the theater a few minutes after the shooting, and was charged with 24 counts of murder and 116 counts of attempted murder. Holmes was sentenced in August 2015 to life in prison without parole for the crime. After the incident, several cast and crew members, including <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a>, <a href="/name/nm0000288">Christian Bale</a>, <a href="/name/nm0004266">Anne Hathaway</a>, <a href="/name/nm0330687">Joseph Gordon-Levitt</a>, and <a href="/name/nm0000198">Gary Oldman</a> released statements expressing their sorrow over the attack. Their publicity appearances, including a lavish premiere in France, were canceled. Warner Brothers decided not to release opening weekend grosses until the following Monday, out of consideration for the victims. Christian Bale went and visited the surviving victims at the hospital several days later.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

  <a name="tr1946800"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
During the film's production in Pittsburgh, a local man was arrested for attempting to steal an unmarked police car; he claimed to authorities that he was only an actor and that his crime was actually a scene for the film. Local newspapers later ran the story with the headline, "Like Batman, car thief's story does not fly."  </div>

  <a name="tr1703161"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> offered <a href="/name/nm0006133">James Newton Howard</a> the opportunity to write the score with <a href="/name/nm0001877">Hans Zimmer</a> as he did for <a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005) and <a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008) but Howard felt that due to the collaboration between Nolan and Zimmer on <a href="/title/tt1375666">Inception</a> (2010), he would be like a third wheel.  </div>

<div id="tr2385926"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2385926"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The Bat Symbol at the beginning of each film in the trilogy foreshadows something that happens later. In this case the Bat Symbol is made up of cracking ice and it symbolizes people falling through the icy river as they are forced to walk across it.  </div>

Selina Kyle's (<a href="/name/nm0004266">Anne Hathaway</a>) relationship with her accomplice (<a href="/name/nm1017334">Juno Temple</a>) is highly reminiscent of Kyle's relationship with Holly Robinson in the comic "Batman: Year One." <div id="tr1533964"

  <a name="tr1533964"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Around 10,000 extras were used to shoot the Gotham Rogues scene in Heinz Field in Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania. Some of the Pittsburgh Steelers played football players: <a href="/name/nm1989961">Hines Ward</a>, <a href="/name/nm2077227">Ben Roethlisberger</a>, <a href="/name/nm2290509">Troy Polamalu</a>, <a href="/name/nm3189164">Willie Colon</a>, <a href="/name/nm4118324">Maurkice Pouncey</a>, <a href="/name/nm3609103">Mike Wallace</a>, <a href="/name/nm2326598">Heath Miller</a>, <a href="/name/nm2287579">Aaron Smith</a>, <a href="/name/nm2398971">Ryan Clark</a>, <a href="/name/nm2294277">James Farrior</a>, <a href="/name/nm3108119">LaMarr Woodley</a>, and <a href="/name/nm2291050">Casey Hampton</a>. Former Steelers coach <a href="/name/nm0184752">Bill Cowher</a> appears as the coach. Pittsburgh mayor <a href="/name/nm3313574">Luke R. Ravenstahl</a> plays a kicker. <a href="/name/nm2100078">Thomas Tull</a>, CEO of the film's production company Legendary Pictures, is part-owner of the Pittsburgh Steelers.  </div>

<div id="tr2002039"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2002039"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In addition to its director, <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a>, The Dark Knight Rises (2012) shares several of its main cast with <a href="/title/tt1375666">Inception</a> (2010): <a href="/name/nm0330687">Joseph Gordon-Levitt</a>, <a href="/name/nm0362766">Tom Hardy</a>, <a href="/name/nm0614165">Cillian Murphy</a>, <a href="/name/nm0182839">Marion Cotillard</a>, and Sir <a href="/name/nm0000323">Michael Caine</a> all appear in both movies, as does Christopher and <a href="/name/nm0634300">Jonathan Nolan</a>'s cousin Miranda in a cameo. Early in the film, when Daggett says of Bruce Wayne "We all know he's up there with eight-inch nails and mason jars full of urine" he's making a reference to billionaire <a href="/name/nm0400652">Howard Hughes</a>, played by <a href="/name/nm0000138">Leonardo DiCaprio</a> in <a href="/title/tt0338751">The Aviator</a> (2004). Nolan also considered making a Hughes biopic at one point.  </div>

With their appearances in this movie, <a href="/name/nm0000288">Christian Bale</a>, Sir <a href="/name/nm0000323">Michael Caine</a>, <a href="/name/nm0000151">Morgan Freeman</a>, <a href="/name/nm0614165">Cillian Murphy</a>, and <a href="/name/nm0000198">Gary Oldman</a> have each appeared in three Batman movies. The Pittsburgh football stadium used in the film was slated for extensive field resurfacing at that time of filming. Explosive squibs were placed to simulate explosion points for the field to collapse. It was Executive Producer <a href="/name/nm2100078">Thomas Tull</a> who gave the film crew access to use the stadium, since he's the co-owner of the Pittsburgh Steelers.  </div>

<div id="tr1281545"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1281545"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Cinematographer <a href="/name/nm0002892">Wally Pfister</a> expressed interest in shooting the entirety of the film in the IMAX format, as both Pfister and <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> expressed distaste for shooting the film in 3-D. Ultimately, the film would feature approximately 72 minutes of IMAX footage, while the rest was shot in a combination of 35mm and 70mm, as IMAX cameras proved to be too noisy for shooting the films dialogue scenes.  </div>

  <div class="sodatext">
The Batman film franchises have attracted the longest list of actors who have Oscar and Golden Globe wins or nominations. 18 Oscars, 34 Golden Globes. The franchises have won 3 Oscars.    <a href="/name/nm0000197">Jack Nicholson</a>  3 Oscars, 9 nominations  7 Golden Globes, 10 Nominations    <a href="/name/nm0000123">George Clooney</a>  2 Oscar, 4 nominations  4 Golden Globes, 7 nominations    Sir <a href="/name/nm0000323">Michael Caine</a>  2 Oscars, 4 nominations  3 Golden Globes, 8 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0000169">Tommy Lee Jones</a>  1 Oscar, 3 nominations  1 Golden Globe, 3 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0000288">Christian Bale</a>  1 Oscar, 2 nominations  1 Golden Globe, 2 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0000932">Halle Berry</a>  1 Oscar  1 Golden Globe, 3 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0005132">Heath Ledger</a> - (only actor to win Oscar/GG for a Batman's character)  1 Oscar, 1 nomination  1 Golden Globe, 1 nomination    <a href="/name/nm0000107">Kim Basinger</a>  1 Oscar  1 Golden Globe, 1 nomination    <a href="/name/nm0000173">Nicole Kidman</a>  1 Oscar, 2 nominations  3 Golden Globes, 6 Nominations    <a href="/name/nm0000255">Ben Affleck</a>  2 Oscars  2 Golden Globes, 1 nomination    <a href="/name/nm0000151">Morgan Freeman</a>  1 Oscar, 3 nominations  2 Golden Globes, 4 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0004266">Anne Hathaway</a>  1 Oscar, 1 nomination  1 Golden Globe, 2 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0182839">Marion Cotillard</a>  1 Oscar, 1 nomination  1 Golden Globe, 2 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0000201">Michelle Pfeiffer</a>  3 Oscar Nominations  1 Golden Globe, 5 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0929489">Tom Wilkinson</a>  2 Oscar nominations  1 Golden Globe, 3 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0000235">Uma Thurman</a>  1 Oscar nomination  1 Golden Globe, 3 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a>  1 Oscar nomination  3 Golden Globe nominations    <a href="/name/nm0000198">Gary Oldman</a>  1 Oscar nomination    <a href="/name/nm0000362">Danny DeVito</a>  1 Oscar nomination  1 Golden Globe, 5 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0350454">Maggie Gyllenhaal</a>  1 Oscar nomination  1 Golden Globe, 2 nominations    <a href="/name/nm0000474">Michael Keaton</a>  1 Oscar nomination  1 Golden Globe, 1 nomination    <a href="/name/nm0362766">Tom Hardy</a>  1 Oscar nomination    <a href="/name/nm0000546">Matthew Modine</a>  2 Golden Globe nominations    <a href="/name/nm0330687">Joseph Gordon-Levitt</a>  2 Golden Globe nominations.    <a href="/name/nm0000120">Jim Carrey</a>  2 Golden Globes, 4 nominations  </div>

<div id="tr2723215"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2723215"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The movie is loosely a reference to Charles Dickens' "A Tale Of Two Cities". This is shown through many details. One being the name of one of the men on trial: Stryver.  </div>

<div id="tr1459349"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1459349"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
There was much speculation in the press, when <a href="/name/nm0004266">Anne Hathaway</a> was announced as Selina Kyle, if the actress would actually portray Kyle's costumed alter-ego, Catwoman. In an interview with <a href="/name/nm0001856">Oprah Winfrey</a>, following her stint as host of the Academy Awards, Hathaway let slip, that her character indeed would don the Catwoman costume.  </div>

<div id="tr1620067"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1620067"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
During the football sequence shown in the trailer, a player is seen wearing a jersey with the last name of Ravenstahl on it. This is <a href="/name/nm3313574">Luke R. Ravenstahl</a>, the Mayor of Pittsburgh, where portions of the movie were shot. He was Washington & Jefferson college's starting place kicker on the football team for three years, and was team Captain for his senior year. He holds the school record for most consecutive extra points.  </div>

<div id="tr1753149"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1753149"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The building used for the exterior of the Gotham Stock Exchange is actually the J.P. Morgan building on the corner of Broad and Wall Streets in lower Manhattan. It is directly across the street from the New York Stock Exchange building, which can be seen in the background in some shots.  </div>

<div id="tr1745839"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1745839"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
When referring to Bruce Wayne as a shut-in, Daggett says "We all know he's up there with eight-inch nails and mason jars full of urine." This is an obvious reference to reclusive and eccentric billionaire <a href="/name/nm0400652">Howard Hughes</a>. <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> was at one point attached to direct a Howard Hughes biopic.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr2239504"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2239504"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Part of the film involves the destruction of a football stadium by Bane. At earlier points, it was considered that this event would be at either a hockey or basketball game, to go along with the demolition of Pittsburgh's now-vacant Civic Arena. Unfortunately, the city of Pittsburgh had difficulties, and a court case in deciding the fate of the arena that, by the time demolition began, filming was finished.  </div>

<div id="tr2969282"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2969282"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Although <a href="/name/nm0002892">Wally Pfister</a> worked on all three Dark Knight films, the styles change drastically from the start of the trilogy. In <a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005), the fight scenes are shot with predominantly shaky-cam technique whereas in this film, the fight scenes are shot very smoothly, with little to no shaky-cam style.  </div>

<div id="tr1747991"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1747991"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The football stadium scene was filmed at Heinz Field, home of the Pittsburgh Steelers. The Steelers' team colors are black and yellow, same as the Gotham Rogues. The fans were also seen twirling yellow rally towels, a nod to the real-life "Terrible Towel" made famous by the Steelers and their long time announcer Myron Cope.  </div>

<div id="tr2546651"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2546651"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Before starring in this film together, <a href="/name/nm0000288">Christian Bale</a> (Batman) and <a href="/name/nm0330687">Joseph Gordon-Levitt</a> (John Blake) had a lot in common with each other, 1. They've both played Jim Hawkins (Bale in <a href="/title/tt0100813">Treasure Island</a> (1990)) and Levitt in <a href="/title/tt0133240">Treasure Planet</a> (2002), they've both done two Disney movies (Bale: <a href="/title/tt0104990">Newsies</a> (1992) and <a href="/title/tt0114148">Pocahontas</a> (1995) and Levitt: <a href="/title/tt0109127">Angels in the Outfield</a> (1994) and <a href="/title/tt0133240">Treasure Planet</a> (2002), their first Disney movies were live-action, and their seconds were animated, and they've already starred in <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> movies prior to this film (Bale: <a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005), <a href="/title/tt0482571">The Prestige</a> (2006) and <a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008) and Levitt: <a href="/title/tt1375666">Inception</a> (2010)).  </div>

<div id="tr1631093"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1631093"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0362766">Tom Hardy</a> is technically the fifth actor to play Bane in a feature film. In <a href="/title/tt0118688">Batman &amp; Robin</a> (1997), <a href="/name/nm0533197">Michael Reid MacKay</a> played serial killer Antonio Diego, who is selected for the "Venom" experiment and is transformed into Bane, who is then played by wrestler <a href="/name/nm0842422">Jeep Swenson</a>. The remaining two actors voiced Bane in two DC Animated direct-to-video films, and they were <a href="/name/nm0001185">Hector Elizondo</a> in <a href="/title/tt0346578">Batman: Mystery of the Batwoman</a> (2003) and <a href="/name/nm0016141">Carlos Alazraqui</a> in <a href="/title/tt2027128">Justice League: Doom</a> (2012).  </div>

  <a name="tr2835070"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
At point of 2012, this movie is the seventh Batman's movie where the budget is more expensive than the previous film. The complete list is this (estimated in dollars):<br /><br />-<a href="/title/tt0060153">Batman: The Movie</a> (1966): $1,377,800.<br /><br />-<a href="/title/tt0096895">Batman</a> (1989): $35,000,000.<br /><br />-<a href="/title/tt0103776">Batman Returns</a> (1992): $80,000,000.<br /><br />-<a href="/title/tt0112462">Batman Forever</a> (1995): $100,000,000.<br /><br />-<a href="/title/tt0118688">Batman &amp; Robin</a> (1997): $125,000,000.<br /><br />-<a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005): $150,000,000.<br /><br />-<a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008): $185,000,000.<br /><br />-<a href="/title/tt1345836">The Dark Knight Rises</a> (2012): $250,000,000.  </div>

<div id="tr1750170"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1750170"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The orphanage, where Blake grew up and visits in the film, is named St. Swithin's. In England, St. Swithin's day takes place on July 15th, and is a tradition where whatever the weather is like on this day, it will be like for the next 40 days, and it is said that if it rains that day it will rain for the next 40. The rhyme goes: "St. Swithin's day if thou dost rain, for forty days it will remain St. Swithin's day if thou be fair, for forty days 'twill rain nae mair." Water and rain are common motifs in <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a>'s films.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a href="?item=tr1750170"
class="interesting-count-text" > 34 of 56 found this interesting</a>

<div id="tr3061164"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3061164"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Christian Bale (Batman) tells Joseph Gordon-Levitt (Officer Blake) to "lead an exodus" of Gotham's people across one of Gotham's bridges, in case their plan fails. This is a reference to the Bible, where Moses leads the enslaved Hebrews out of Egypt, and into there promised land. Christian Bale later plays Moses in Ridley Scott's Exodus: Gods and Kings (2014).  </div>

<div id="tr3254201"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3254201"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In 2017, during his inaugration speech, The President of the United States, Donald Trump, quoted part of Bane's Blackgate Prison speech. He quoted the line, "To you, the people!". This caused much amusement as several people compared his political agenda for the United States as to that of Bane's of Gotham.  </div>

  <a name="tr1790609"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0634297">John Nolan</a>: The uncle of director <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> and co-writer <a href="/name/nm0634300">Jonathan Nolan</a>, as well as the father of <a href="/name/nm3886541">Miranda Nolan</a>, reprises his role from <a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005) as Wayne Enterprises board member Douglas Fredericks. He previously appeared in Christopher's debut film, <a href="/title/tt0154506">Following</a> (1998).  </div>

  <a name="tr1916449"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In the early minutes of each film in the trilogy, the main villain (Ra's Al Ghul, Joker, Bane) disguises himself as one of his own henchmen and there is a conversation about said villain in each scene.  </div>

In all three movies, Batman repeats a line of dialogue spoken to him by one of the villains. In this film, he tells Bane, "You have my permission to die."  </div>

<div id="tr2089028"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2089028"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
For the final scene at the Wayne family cemetery, a tombstone with the name "Miranda Tate" was used during filming to conceal the actual ending to the film. The name on the stone was changed to "Bruce Wayne" via digital technology in post-production.  </div>

<div id="tr2094849"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2094849"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The final shooting script features several deleted/extended scenes not found in the film. Most are "character moments" though some also clarify details of the plot. They include: <ul><li>A scene at Wayne Manor where the Congressman tells Foley that he's next in line for the role of Police Commissioner if he does well, giving Foley one more incentive of chasing Batman for the murder of Harvey Dent other than Batman being public enemy number one, ;</li><br /><br /><li>A conversation between the two thugs that capture Commissioner Gordon where they debate killing him before taking him to Bane (giving a direct explanation on how Gordon learned Bane's name)</li><br /><br /><li>A scene at Wayne Enterprises where Miranda warns Lucius Fox that Daggett is trying to take control of the company;</li><br /><br /><li>A longer scene of Bruce Wayne and Lucius Fox at the Applied Sciences warehouse in which Fox wants to give Wayne the special leg brace which allows him to walk again;</li><br /><br /><li>Bruce testing the leg brace in the Batcave, explaining to Alfred how it works to match the muscle patterns of his uninjured leg;</li><br /><br /><li>A longer and slightly different scene outside the stock exchange and a lengthy chase scene between Bane, the police and Batman where they race around Gotham. The script has the stock exchange scenes all occurring in the evening instead of the late afternoon as the film had started at;</li><br /><br /><li>An argument in the Batcave between Bruce and Alfred revealing that Bruce bought up all the land and homes surrounding Wayne Manor to prevent anyone from seeing him coming and going as Batman;</li><br /><br /><li>An extended, much more heated confrontation between Bruce and Alfred. Alfred threatens to leave Wayne Manor if Bruce continues as Batman and Bruce argues that since Rachel Dawes's death, Batman is his only reason to live. Alfred confesses that he burned Rachel's letter and lied about her choosing to marry Bruce. Bruce accuses Alfred of betrayal before Alfred gives his speech about protecting Bruce's life, which does appear in the final film;</li><br /><br /><li>A longer conversation between Bruce, Miranda & Fox discussing the reactor and Dr. Pavel;</li><br /><br /><li>An extended conversation between Bruce & Blake in Blake's care where Blake jokingly gives Bruce cash for cab fare.</li><br /><br /><li>A much extended scene of Bane storming Blackgate Prison. Bane burns a picture of Harvey Dent and explains that Dent became the villain Two-Face after his injuries and encourages the city's poor to attack the wealthy and powerful before he destroys Blackgate, releasing all the inmates;</li><br /><br /><li>A brief scene of Selina escaping Blackgate;</li><br /><br /><li>A series of extended or omitted scenes showing the mercenaries seeing the burning Bat-signal on Gotham Bridge.</li><br /><br /><li>An extensive flashback sequence after Batman defeats Bane. Bane confesses that his devotion to Ra's Al Guhl stems from the League of Shadows rescuing him from the pit. A flashback scene then shows Ra's Al Guhl training Bane, who he has provided with a crude prototype mask to numb his pain;</li><br /><br /><li>A scene of Talia openly taking charge of the League of Shadows to form a convoy to detonate the neutron bomb. She then floods the reactor core and, as in the film, Fox tries to escape, though even the finished scenes of Fox in the film occur earlier in the script version;</li><br /><br /><li>A longer argument between Blake and the Army blockade on Gotham Bridge. Blake argues with the commanding officer, trying to convince him that Batman has returned and battle has broken out in the city streets.</li><br /><br /><li>In the script, after Batman harnesses the bomb to The Bat, he's never seen again--The Bat simply flies out to sea and the bomb detonates. The scene of Fox and the technicians examining the autopilot of The Bat then follows, with Fox realizing that Batman had ejected before the bomb detonated, and that Bruce Wayne must have survived the explosion.</li><br /><br /></ul>  </div>

<div id="tr1254584"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1254584"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000288">Christian Bale</a> has stated that he would not play Batman if Robin appeared anywhere in the trilogy. <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> agreed not to include Robin as it would undermine the dark tone of his series. At the end of the film, Detective John Blake's (<a href="/name/nm0330687">Joseph Gordon-Levitt</a>) legal name is revealed to be "Robin", and he quits the police force and is shown to enter the Batcave by following the instructions presumably left by Bruce Wayne in his will.  </div>

<div id="tr1756919"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1756919"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In a final bit of foreshadowing as to her character's true nature, Miranda Tate, after Bruce apologizes for being unable to get her out of the city, tells Bruce to "do what is necessary." Her father, Ra's al Ghul, repeatedly derides Bruce for lacking "the courage to do what is necessary" in <a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005)  </div>

<div id="tr1775457"

  <a name="tr1775457"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
There are several moments in the film where it is hinted that the child was not Bane. Bane tells Batman he never saw light, until he was already a man. Furthermore, the child that escapes from the pit, is not scarred, despite the fact we know Bane was treated within the prison.  </div>

<div id="tr1759835"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1759835"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In all three Nolan Batman films, the spiked gauntlets on Batman's arms prove essential in defeating the main villain. They shatter Ra's al Ghul's sword in <a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005), knock the detonator out of the Joker's hands in <a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008) and damage Bane's mask in The Dark Knight Rises (2012).  </div>

<div id="tr1748292"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1748292"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The villainous character portrayed by <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> Ra's al Ghul, who died by the end of the first movie, makes an appearance before Bruce Wayne's eyes, claiming to be immortal the whole time, only to be revealed as a hallucination. This is a reference to Ra's al Ghul's comic book counterpart, in which the character IS immortal, by the use of Lazarus Pits.  </div>

<div id="tr1744251"

  <a name="tr1744251"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
During the fight between Bane and Batman in the sewers, Bane lifts Batman above his head and drops him across his knee. This is a direct parallel to the first fight between Batman and Bane from the comics, where Bane broke Batman's back during the "Knightfall" story line.  </div>

<div id="tr1885486"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1885486"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Some viewers found the scene at the end of the movie ambiguous, in which Alfred sees Bruce and Selina at a café. While some took it at face value (that Bruce survived and Alfred really saw him), others thought that Bruce was dead, and saw the café scene as a non-literal fantasy nod to Alfred's stated wish from earlier in the movie that Bruce might be able to someday find peace, and a normal life. In a December 2012 interview with the Los Angeles Times, Sir <a href="/name/nm0000323">Michael Caine</a> seemed to settle the question when he said that Bruce was supposed to be unambiguously alive during the scene: "They were there....They were real. There was no imagination. They were real and he was with <a href="/name/nm0004266">Anne Hathaway</a> (who played Selina Kyle), the cat lady, and I was happy ever after for him as I told him during the picture." Furthermore, the film's shooting script also specifies, that Bruce is alive during the café scene. A line of spoken dialogue towards the end of the film, also notes that Martha Wayne's pearls are missing from the Wayne estate. In the final scene, Selina is seen wearing the necklace.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr1748269"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1748269"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In the film there are a total of five Oscar winners: <a href="/name/nm0000288">Christian Bale</a>, Sir <a href="/name/nm0000323">Michael Caine</a>, <a href="/name/nm0000151">Morgan Freeman</a>, <a href="/name/nm0182839">Marion Cotillard</a>, <a href="/name/nm0004266">Anne Hathaway</a>, and three Oscar nominees: <a href="/name/nm0000198">Gary Oldman</a>, <a href="/name/nm0002018">Tom Conti</a>, <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a>. Additionally, Oscar nominee <a href="/name/nm0350454">Maggie Gyllenhaal</a> appears in archive footage, bringing the total nominees to nine, unprecedented in a comic book film.  </div>

<div id="tr1698530"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1698530"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The original story treatment by <a href="/name/nm0333060">David S. Goyer</a>, as outlined before the production of <a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005), was to have Two-Face as the principal antagonist for the film. Initially, at the end of <a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008), the Joker would have scarred Harvey Dent at a courtroom trial, setting up the third film. Dent's death and fall was put in at the end of the second film instead, to set up the aftermath that follows. Following the release of this film, Nolan elaborated on his choice to include the Two-Face story in the prior film: he wanted each movie to stand on its own as a complete story, and not "tease" any sequels--a practice that had become common amongst comic book films. Nolan feels that holding back story or leaving a film open-ended for a sequel, on which to build, is a cheat to the audience, which deserves to see a movie that has consumed all of the filmmakers' creative energy.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr1590417"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1590417"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In the comics, Bane carried an apparatus that contains a steroid that amplifies his strength and fighting ability. In the film, the apparatus he carries contains an anesthetic, as he is in chronic pain. In both the comics and the film, Batman defeats Bane in a similar way, by damaging his mask, depriving him of the drug.  </div>

According to The Hollywood Reporter, <a href="/name/nm0004266">Anne Hathaway</a>'s stunt double broke one of the IMAX cameras when she crashed the Batpod into it. This marks the second time an IMAX camera has been destroyed on a <a href="/name/nm0634240">Christopher Nolan</a> Batman film - a previous camera was smashed when filming the Joker's underground truck chase in <a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008).  </div>

<div id="tr1430574"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1430574"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm1200692">Eva Green</a>, <a href="/name/nm0915208">Naomi Watts</a>, <a href="/name/nm0001838">Rachel Weisz</a>, and <a href="/name/nm0000701">Kate Winslet</a> were considered to play Miranda Tate, before <a href="/name/nm0182839">Marion Cotillard</a> finally got the role in February 2011, when she was six months pregnant. Cotillard started filming one month after she gave birth to her son, Marcel. In October 2010, it was reported that she had turned down the roles of Catwoman and Talia Al Ghul in the film, but as of 2016, there is no official confirmation that she was considered to play Catwoman.  </div>

<div id="tr1983606"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1983606"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
John Blake's real name, Robin, is an allusion to the character in Batman comic books, movies, and television shows. Robin was added to the Batman comic books in 1940, to attract younger readers, and the character eventually evolved into a solo superhero, Nightwing. Blake, though an original character, combines elements of the various Robins from the comics - an orphan (like Dick Grayson), a street kid (like Jason Todd), and a skilled detective who deduces Batman's true identity (like Tim Drake), all of whom trained as Batman's sidekick, with the implication that they one day would don the Batman costume.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr1742585"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1742585"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
According to <a href="/name/nm0634300">Jonathan Nolan</a>, a major influence on the story is <a href="/name/nm0002042">Charles Dickens</a>'s socio-political novel "A Tale of Two Cities", which dealt with revolution and class conflict. In an homage to the story, two characters in the film are named Stryver and Barsad, after two similarly named characters in the book. Also, when Commissioner Gordon gives a eulogy for Bruce, he uses the ending soliloquy in regards to Batman, who, like the novel's hero Sydney Carton, sacrificed himself to save people.  </div>

<div id="tr1590418"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1590418"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The filmmakers cite the "Batman" comics 'The Dark Knight Returns' (an aged Batman operates in a future Gotham), 'Knightfall' (Bane pushes Batman physically and mentally, causing him to burn out) and 'No Man's Land' (Gotham descends into post-apocalyptic gangland territory, and is cut off from the rest of the U.S.) as major influences on the film.  </div>

<div id="tr2640150"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2640150"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In each part of the trilogy, Batman/Bruce Wayne has either a friend who turns into the villain or vice versa:    -<a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005): Ra's Al Ghul trains Bruce Wayne, and then turns against him.    -<a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008): Harvey Dent a.k.a. Two-Face is an ally of Bruce Wayne, then afterwards, opposes Batman, blaming him for Rachel's death, and his transformation.    -<a href="/title/tt1345836">The Dark Knight Rises</a> (2012): Catwoman/Selina Kyle initially steals from Bruce Wayne (Lamborghini and necklace), then tricks him into Banes underground hiding. Near the end she sides with Batman over Bane.    Also, Miranda is initially an ally of Bruce Wayne and Wayne Enterprises. Near the end, she reveals herself to be a villain all along.  </div>

This marks the second trilogy of movies in which <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> plays a character who is killed in the first movie, only to subsequently return incorporeally to communicate with a central character in a later movie (the other trilogy being the Star Wars prequels.)  </div>

<div id="tr1761539"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1761539"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Though not shown in the final cut, the fight scene on Gotham City Hall steps, included an explosion that cleared the steps of all the fighters still alive. When filming the actual explosion, the heat triggered a fire alarm, that went directly to the authorities; which caused production to stop for more than thirty minutes, while the film staff cleared everything with the police and Fire Marshal when they arrived.  </div>

<div id="tr1744826"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1744826"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The first Batman movie not to feature Batman driving the Batmobile. He only uses the Bat-pod and the Bat (flying vehicle). While several variations of Tumblers do make an appearance, they are all operated by Bane and his thugs, after they steal them from Wayne Enterprises' Applied Science Division, and these have a desert camouflage paint job, so it could be argued that the Batmobile doesn't make any appearance at all.  </div>

<div id="tr2556737"

  <a name="tr2556737"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
When Officer Blake mentions giant alligators in the sewers, this is a reference to Killer Croc (who makes his big-screen debut in Suicide Squad (2016)). In the comics, Killer Croc has clashed with Bane, the main villain. Bane broke both of Croc's arms, before fighting Batman and breaking his back.  </div>

<div id="tr2549982"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2549982"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The only time Bane shoots a gun in the movie, is at one of his henchmen in the sewer. The other time he tries to use a gun, is when he attempts to kill Batman before he's killed by Catwoman on the Batpod.  </div>

<div id="tr2996710"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2996710"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The same musical cue is used in all three movies of The Dark Knight Trilogy when Batman deals the final blow to his main adversary. All three of these moments involve gravity getting the best of the villain. The train careens off the tracks in <a href="/title/tt0372784">Batman Begins</a> (2005) with Raz Al-Ghul inside. The Joker falls off the Pruitt Building in <a href="/title/tt0468569">The Dark Knight</a> (2008), and Talia Al'Ghul drives off the upper level of Grand Avenue in <a href="/title/tt1345836">The Dark Knight Rises</a> (2012).  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr3026625"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3026625"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The entrance to the Batcave, shown in the ending sequence, when Blake is following the instructions, was shot in Wales, <a href="/name/nm0000288">Christian Bale</a>'s home country.  </div>

<div id="tr2296846"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2296846"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Batman tells Blake to get as many Gothamites out of the city before the bomb goes off, that "We need an exodus". <a href="/name/nm0000288">Christian Bale</a> later played Moses in <a href="/title/tt1528100">Exodus: Gods and Kings</a> (2014), based upon the biblical book of Exodus.  </div>

<div id="tr2527669"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2527669"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In the football scene, the surviving player has the name Ward on his shirt. In the <a href="/title/tt0059968">Batman</a> (1966) television series, Robin was played by <a href="/name/nm0911431">Burt Ward</a>. The surviving player's real-life name is <a href="/name/nm1989961">Hines Ward</a>.  </div>

<div id="tr3261384"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3261384"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In this film <a href="/name/nm0182839">Marion Cotillard</a>'s character is trying to destroy the city using the atomic bomb. Interestingly, the next blockbuster starring Cotillard, <a href="/title/tt2094766">Assassin's Creed</a> (2016), is having her character quoting J. Robert Oppenheimer, one of the creators of the atom bomb, by saying "Now I am become death, the destroyer of worlds".  </div>
